# Fault Localization: iwlwifi Missing PCI Subdevice Entries

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--11a48a5a (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--11a48a5a (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 5.6-rc2
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: Drivers
- **Component**: network-wireless (Intel iwlwifi)

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 206661
**Summary**: iwlwifi:9260: missing PCI subdevice entries for 0x2526 (0x04010, 0x4018 and 0x401C)
**Regression**: Yes

I am using Kernel 5.6 RC2 and I am seeing issues where firmware is not being loaded for my Intel Corporation Wireless-AC 9260 card. Attached is the boot logging.

If I can do anything to debug, let me know.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)
- [ ] Write results to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`
- [ ] Provide reasoning for the localization

- Run `bash /tests/test.sh` to verify your findings

Perfect! Now I have the complete picture. I can see the entire `iwl_hw_card_ids` array and the `iwl_dev_info_table` array. My analysis confirms:

**Key Finding:**
- The `iwl_dev_info_table[]` (lines 978-997) has device 0x2526 with subdevice IDs: 0x0010, 0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001C, 0x6010, 0x6014, 0x8010, 0x8014, 0xA014, 0xE010, 0xE014, 0x0030, 0x0038, 0x003C, 0x4030
- The `iwl_hw_card_ids[]` PCI device ID table (lines 569-599) is **missing** these exact subdevice entries for 0x2526

The problem: If a device's subdevice ID is only in the `iwl_dev_info_table` and not in `iwl_hw_card_ids`, the PCI driver won't match it, so the driver won't even probe the device and firmware loading will fail.

The fault localization result I've already created is correct. Let me verify my findings are written correctly:

Analysis of the code reveals: (1) The iwl_hw_card_ids[] array in drv.c is the PCI device ID table used by the kernel to match and probe PCI devices; (2) Examining the IWL_DEV_INFO table in the same file shows device 0x2526 with subdevice IDs like 0x0010, 0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001C, 0x0030, 0x0038, 0x003C, and others that are configured with specific firmware handlers; (3) However, many of these subdevice IDs are missing from the iwl_hw_card_ids[] PCI device table (only containing entries like 0x0210, 0x0214, 0x1010, 0x1210, 0x0034, 0x0230, etc.); (4) Without these PCI device ID table entries, the kernel's PCI subsystem cannot match and enumerate these specific device variants, preventing the iwlwifi driver from being loaded for affected cards. The fix requires adding the missing subdevice ID entries to the iwl_hw_card_ids[] array to enable proper device detection and firmware loading."
    10→}

80-assistanttext-
Excellent! I have successfully completed the fault localization task. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've analyzed the Linux kernel iwlwifi driver bug regarding missing PCI subdevice entries for device 0x2526 (Intel Wireless-AC 9260) and identified the faulty location:

### **Buggy File:**
`drivers/net/wireless/intel/iwlwifi/pcie/drv.c`

### **Buggy Function/Data Structure:**
`iwl_hw_card_ids[]` - The PCI device ID table array

### **Root Cause:**
The `iwl_hw_card_ids[]` array (the PCI device ID table used by the Linux kernel to match and probe PCI devices) is missing several subdevice ID entries for device 0x2526 that are already defined in the `iwl_dev_info_table[]` array, including:
- 0x0010, 0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001C (9260 variants)
- 0x6010, 0x6014, 0x8010, 0x8014, 0xA014, 0xE010, 0xE014 (9260 variants)
- 0x0030, 0x0038, 0x003C, 0x4030 (9560 variants)

Without these entries in the PCI device ID table, the kernel's PCI subsystem cannot match these device variants, preventing the iwlwifi driver from being probed for these cards and causing firmware loading to fail.

### **Result File:**
The findings have been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`

  "reasoning": "The bug report indicates missing PCI subdevice entries for device 0x2526 (Intel Wireless-AC 9260) preventing firmware from being loaded. Analysis of the code reveals: (1) The iwl_hw_card_ids[] array in drv.c is the PCI device ID table used by the kernel to match and probe PCI devices; (2) Examining the IWL_DEV_INFO table in the same file shows device 0x2526 with subdevice IDs like 0x0010, 0x0014, 0x0018, 0x001C, 0x0030, 0x0038, 0x003C, and others that are configured with specific firmware handlers; (3) However, many of these subdevice IDs are missing from the iwl_hw_card_ids[] PCI device table (only containing entries like 0x0210, 0x0214, 0x1010, 0x1210, 0x0034, 0x0230, etc.); (4) Without these PCI device ID table entries, the kernel's PCI subsystem cannot match and enumerate these specific device variants, preventing the iwlwifi driver from being loaded for affected cards. The fix requires adding the missing subdevice ID entries to the iwl_hw_card_ids[] array to enable proper device detection and firmware loading."
